Inside the reactor, it is difficult to completely understand the situation, in advance avoid contact with obstacles. The coupled tendon-driven articulated arm \u2018Super Dragon\u2019 can achieve high endpoint compliance without special control thanks to the elasticity of synthetic fiber ropes used for driving, making it highly adaptable to unknown environments for investigation purposes. This paper aims to demonstrate the high environmental adaptability of coupled tendon-driven arms. We showed the arm&#039;s endpoint compliance through numerical analysis and hardware experiments. Furthermore, leveraging this compliance, we achieved external contact detection using measured tension and joint torque decrease.",

The coupled tendon-driven articulated arm \u2018Super Dragon\u2019 can achieve high endpoint compliance without special control thanks to the elasticity of synthetic fiber ropes used for driving, making it highly adaptable to unknown environments for investigation purposes. This paper aims to demonstrate the high environmental adaptability of coupled tendon-driven arms. We showed the arm&#039;s endpoint compliance through numerical analysis and hardware experiments.                             <div id="mathJaxToggle"><label for="mathJaxToggle"><span>Formulae display:</span><input type="checkbox" id="mathJaxToggleCheck" name="mathJaxToggleCheck"></label><span class="mathJaxLogo"><img src="/templates/jsp/_style2/_tandf/pb2/images/math-jax.gif" loading="lazy" alt="MathJax Logo"><span data-tooltip-wrapper=""><span class="qMrk" data-behaviour="tooltip">?</span><span class="auPopUp" data-tooltip=""><span class="pointyEdge"></span>Mathematical formulae have been encoded as MathML and are displayed in this HTML version using MathJax in order to improve their display. Uncheck the box to turn MathJax off. This feature requires Javascript. Click on a formula to zoom.</span></span></span></div><div class="hlFld-Fulltext"><div id="abstractId1" class="hlFld-Abstract"><h2 class="section-heading-2" id="abstract">Abstract</h2><p class="first last">For decommissioning work at the Fukushima Daiichi Nuclear Power Station, internal investigation using long-reach articulated arms is required. Inside the reactor, it is difficult to completely understand the situation, in advance avoid contact with obstacles. The coupled tendon-driven articulated arm ‘Super Dragon’ can achieve high endpoint compliance without special control thanks to the elasticity of synthetic fiber ropes used for driving, making it highly adaptable to unknown environments for investigation purposes. This paper aims to demonstrate the high environmental adaptability of coupled tendon-driven arms. We showed the arm's endpoint compliance through numerical analysis and hardware experiments. Furthermore, leveraging this compliance, we achieved external contact detection using measured tension and joint torque decrease.</p></div><div id="abstractId2" class="hlFld-Abstract"><h2 class="section-heading-2" id="graphical-abstract">GRAPHICAL ABSTRACT</h2><div class="figureView"><a href="#" class="thumbnail" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-popup-event-type="fig" data-id="UF0001" aria-label="thumbnail image"><img id="d1e148" src="/cms/asset/16df7fb5-0ff6-4660-932d-1768402fea49/tadr_a_2642632_uf0001_oc.jpg" loading="lazy" height="452" width="500"></a><div><button class="show-full-size btn btn-sm" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-id="UF0001" data-popup-event-type="fig">Display full size</button></div></div></div><div class="abstractKeywords"><div class="hlFld-KeywordText"><div><p id="kwd-title-d16624139e150" class="kwd-title">Keywords: </p><ul aria-labelledby="kwd-title-d16624139e150"><li><a href="/keyword/Long-reach+articulated+arm" class="kwd-btn keyword-click">Long-reach articulated arm</a></li><li><a href="/keyword/coupled+tendon+drive" class="kwd-btn keyword-click">coupled tendon drive</a></li><li><a href="/keyword/endpoint+compliance" class="kwd-btn keyword-click">endpoint compliance</a></li><li><a href="/keyword/synthetic+fiber+rope" class="kwd-btn keyword-click">synthetic fiber rope</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div id="embedded-pdf-target" class="with-border"></div><div class="pb-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="contentNavigationDropZoneAbs"><div class="widget gql-content-navigation none  widget-none" id="2ffb43c7-15dc-4c79-9e29-8e4bed9b3d1e">
        
        

        <div class="wrapped ">
            
            <div class="widget-body body body-none "><div class="ajaxWidget" data-ajax-widget="gql-content-navigation" data-ajax-widget-id="2ffb43c7-15dc-4c79-9e29-8e4bed9b3d1e" data-ajax-observe="true">
    
</div></div>
        </div>
    </div></div><div class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1" id="S001"><h2 class="section-heading-2" id="d1e175">1.  Introduction</h2><p>For the decommissioning work of the Fukushima Daiichi Nuclear Power Station, internal investigation of the Primary Containment Vessel (PCV) is required. To achieve internal investigation of the PCV, which is a high-radiation area, an investigation method has been proposed where an articulated arm equipped with investigation equipment at the tip penetrates into the PCV for exploration, and various articulated arms have been developed [<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref bibr"><a data-rid="CIT0001 CIT0002 CIT0003 CIT0004 CIT0005" href="#" data-behaviour="toggle-ref" data-ref-type="bibr" data-label="reference"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>1–5</a></span>]. In this method, the arm is required to be long-reach and slim to pass through narrow spaces and investigate vast areas, as well as have a large payload to carry investigation equipment.</p><p>We believe that adaptability to unknown environments is necessary in addition to these conditions. While typical robotic arm exploration work requires precise control to avoid obstacles, in PCV investigation, it is difficult to avoid contact with the external environment as the internal situation cannot be grasped in advance. Therefore, we consider that an articulated arm with a certain degree of compliance would be useful to prevent damage when the arm contacts the external environment. However, to the best of our knowledge, there are no prior studies on articulated arms for decommissioning work that focus on adaptability during external contact.</p><p>We have developed Super Dragon (Figure&nbsp;<button class="ref show-table-fig-ref" data-id="F0001" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-popup-event-type="fig">1</button>), a coupled tendon-driven super long-reach articulated arm [<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref bibr"><a data-rid="CIT0006 CIT0007 CIT0008 CIT0009 CIT0010" href="#" data-behaviour="toggle-ref" data-ref-type="bibr" data-label="reference"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>6–10</a></span>]. Generally, as robot arms become longer, their mass increases, making it difficult to develop arms that are both long-reach and slim. However, coupled tendon drive can achieve long-reach, lightweight, and large payload by placing actuators at the base and supporting the root joints, which apply the largest gravity torque, through coupled drive [<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref bibr"><a data-rid="CIT0011" href="#" data-behaviour="toggle-ref" data-ref-type="bibr" data-label="reference"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>11</a></span>]. In this paper, in addition to these advantages, we focus on the feature that compliance can be achieved without special control due to the elasticity of the synthetic fiber ropes used for driving. In the literature, Series Elastic Actuators (SEAs) intentionally incorporate elastic elements into actuators to achieve compliance through mechanical elasticity rather than active actuator control [<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref bibr"><a data-rid="CIT0012" href="#" data-behaviour="toggle-ref" data-ref-type="bibr" data-label="reference"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>12</a></span>]. SEAs improve impact resistance by low-pass filtering impact loads through their elastic elements, and this effectiveness has been verified using a geared motor incorporating a torsion spring as the elastic element. In our case, we believe that long-path synthetic fiber ropes, such as those used in this study, can also serve as elastic elements. In other words, it is considered possible to allow contact between the arm itself and the external environment while penetrating without destroying the arm. Furthermore, since the base is equipped with tension sensors for the driving tendons, we believe that contact with the external environments can be detected without special equipment by utilizing the change in tension during external contact. Moreover, if contact between the arm and the external environment is allowed, it is considered possible to reduce joint torque by intentionally contact the arm to the external environment to support the gravity. In other words, there is a possibility of achievement of operations that intentionally exploit contact between the arm and the external environment.
</p><div class="figureView"><div class="short-legend"><p class="captionText"><span aria-level="3" role="heading"><span class="captionLabel">Figure 1. </span></span> Ten meter long coupled tendon-driven articulated arm ‘Super Dragon’ [<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref bibr"><a data-rid="CIT0003 CIT0004 CIT0005" href="#" data-behaviour="toggle-ref" data-ref-type="bibr" data-label="reference"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>3–5</a></span>].</p></div><a href="#" class="thumbnail" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-popup-event-type="fig" data-id="F0001"><img id="d1e208" src="/cms/asset/f837fdd3-3216-47c3-93af-a9b31a53f771/tadr_a_2642632_f0001_oc.jpg" loading="lazy" height="388" width="500" alt="Figure 1. Ten meter long coupled tendon-driven articulated arm ‘Super Dragon’ [Citation3–5]."></a><div><button class="show-full-size btn btn-sm" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-id="F0001" data-popup-event-type="fig">Display full size</button></div></div><p></p><p class="last">Therefore, this paper aims to demonstrate the high external environment adaptability of coupled tendon-driven arms in unknown environments. First, we will show through analysis and hardware experiments that coupled tendon-driven arms have high compliance due to the elongation of driving tendons. Additionally, by comparing analytical and measured values, we discuss the extent to which the analysis can be applied. Then, through hardware experiments, we will achieve three points: contact with the external environment without damage to the arm or obstacles, the possibility of detecting external contact, and operations that utilize external contact.</p></div><div class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1" id="S002"><h2 class="section-heading-2" id="d1e212">2.  Super Dragon</h2><p>This section explains the coupled tendon drive, which is the driving method of Super&nbsp;Dragon, and the hardware, respectively.</p><div class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2" id="S002-S2001"><h3 class="section-heading-3" id="d1e217">2.1.  Coupled tendon drive</h3><p>Coupled tendon drive is a driving method for long-reach manipulators proposed by Hirose et&nbsp;al. which drives each joint using tendons such as metal wires or ropes [<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref bibr"><a data-rid="CIT0011" href="#" data-behaviour="toggle-ref" data-ref-type="bibr" data-label="reference"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>11</a></span>]. Figure&nbsp;<button class="ref show-table-fig-ref" data-id="F0002" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-popup-event-type="fig">2</button> shows a coupled tendon-driven manipulator composed of three joints. The joint located closest to the base is called the 1st joint, and from there toward the tip, they are called the 2nd joint, 3rd joint, and so on.
</p><div class="figureView"><div class="short-legend"><p class="captionText"><span aria-level="3" role="heading"><span class="captionLabel">Figure 2. </span></span> Coupled tendon-driven articulated arm.</p></div><a href="#" class="thumbnail" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-popup-event-type="fig" data-id="F0002"><img id="d1e235" src="/cms/asset/94bf712c-8c7a-4184-b917-eeadd7f58084/tadr_a_2642632_f0002_oc.jpg" loading="lazy" height="275" width="500" alt="Figure 2. Coupled tendon-driven articulated arm."></a><div><button class="show-full-size btn btn-sm" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-id="F0002" data-popup-event-type="fig">Display full size</button></div></div><p></p><p class="last">Each joint has a pulley fixed to the link (hereinafter driving pulley), to which the end of the tendon driving that joint is fixed. Tendons driving joints on the tip side are wound around joints on the base side via freely rotating pulleys (hereinafter torque transmission pulleys). When all pulley radii are equal to <i>r</i> and each tendon is pulled with force <i>F</i>, the torques generated at each joint are <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/6c24ccce-d433-41e2-bf4b-941342d751ee/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0001.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><msub><mi>τ</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>=</mo><mn>3</mn><mi>Fr</mi></math></span>, <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/8bab9fbf-a64e-4e63-beee-41567e87f159/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0002.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><msub><mi>τ</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>=</mo><mn>2</mn><mi>Fr</mi></math></span>, and <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/66cfde89-df58-4b95-bb91-87c69cfa25bb/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0003.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><msub><mi>τ</mi><mn>3</mn></msub><mo>=</mo><mi>Fr</mi></math></span> from the base, respectively. Thus, joints closer to the base, which require larger torque to support gravity, have more tendons wound around them, enabling the generation of larger torque. Furthermore, by mounting the actuators that pull the tendons at the base rather than on the arm, the arm portion can be made lightweight. In this way, coupled tendon drive is suitable as a driving method for long-reach manipulators because it can support the arm's gravity with the tension of multiple tendons.</p></div><div class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2" id="S002-S2002"><h3 class="section-heading-3" id="d1e281">2.2.  Hardware</h3><p>We explain the hardware configuration of Super Dragon. Super&nbsp;Dragon is a coupled tendon-driven manipulator with an arm length of 10 m, maximum arm diameter of 0.2 m, and 10 joints [<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref bibr"><a data-rid="CIT0006 CIT0007 CIT0008 CIT0009 CIT0010" href="#" data-behaviour="toggle-ref" data-ref-type="bibr" data-label="reference"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>6–10</a></span>]. The arrangement of joints, tendons, and pulleys of Super&nbsp;Dragon is shown in Figure&nbsp;<button class="ref show-table-fig-ref" data-id="F0003" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-popup-event-type="fig">3</button>. In this paper, we define yaw joints whose axes coincide with the vertical direction when the arm is extended horizontally, and pitch joints whose axes are horizontal and perpendicular to the longitudinal direction. We consider an <i>xyz</i> coordinate system, with the vertically upward direction as the positive <i>z</i>-axis direction, and the direction from the base to the tip when the arm takes a horizontal posture as the positive <i>x</i>-axis direction. This arm consists of pitch joints and yaw joints, enabling three-dimensional motion through three-dimensional coupled tendon drive [<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref bibr"><a data-rid="CIT0013" href="#" data-behaviour="toggle-ref" data-ref-type="bibr" data-label="reference"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>13</a></span>]. In Figure <button class="ref show-table-fig-ref" data-id="F0003" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-popup-event-type="fig">3</button>, tendons driving pitch joints are shown in pink, and tendons driving yaw joints are shown in cyan. Additionally, Horigome et&nbsp;al. proposed a gravity compensation mechanism for arms using large-diameter tendons introduced separately from the coupled tendon drive system, which Super&nbsp;Dragon adopts [<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref bibr"><a data-rid="CIT0014" href="#" data-behaviour="toggle-ref" data-ref-type="bibr" data-label="reference"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>14</a></span>]. This method compensates for most of the gravity by winding a large-diameter tendon shown in orange in Figure <button class="ref show-table-fig-ref" data-id="F0003" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-popup-event-type="fig">3</button> around pitch joints and pulling it with actuators with large generating force such as pneumatic cylinders, in addition to the tendons that control each joint. In this paper, we refer to the small-diameter tendons that control joints as joint control tendons and the large-diameter tendons that compensate for gravity as gravity compensation tendons.
</p><div class="figureView"><div class="short-legend"><p class="captionText"><span aria-level="3" role="heading"><span class="captionLabel">Figure 3. </span></span> Joint configuration and tendon-pulley arrangement. Magenta and cyan lines represent joint control tendons of pitch and yaw joints respectively. Orange line represent gravity compensation tendon.</p></div><a href="#" class="thumbnail" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-popup-event-type="fig" data-id="F0003"><img id="d1e321" src="/cms/asset/0db151a0-4ea1-44e6-bc06-4cc934e805b8/tadr_a_2642632_f0003_oc.jpg" loading="lazy" height="396" width="500" alt="Figure 3. Joint configuration and tendon-pulley arrangement. Magenta and cyan lines represent joint control tendons of pitch and yaw joints respectively. Orange line represent gravity compensation tendon."></a><div><button class="show-full-size btn btn-sm" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-id="F0003" data-popup-event-type="fig">Display full size</button></div></div><p></p><p class="last">The joint control tendons use 2 mm diameter ropes (NA20020SOC00\001.000, Armare) made of high-density polyethylene with heat-set. For gravity compensation tendons, 5.5 mm diameter PBO fiber rope (ZB-15728, Hayami Industry) is used, wound from the 1st joint to the 5th joint. Each joint is equipped with a potentiometer (JC10-000-103N, Nidec Copal Electronics), allowing the arm's posture to be acquired at each control cycle. The base is equipped with gear-head electromagnetic motors (241322, Maxon Motor) that pull the joint control tendons, pneumatic cylinders (10A-2FB200B300, TAIYO) that pull the gravity compensation tendons, tension sensors, and other electrical systems. Joint angle control is performed by PI control of the winding amount of joint control tendons, and for gravity compensation tendons, PI control of the pressure value of the pneumatic cylinders that apply tension is performed. Super Dragon can generate high joint torque due to the characteristics of coupled tendon drive, which enables arm weight reduction and allows the arm's self-weight to be cooperatively supported by multiple tendons. For example, in an experiment maintaining a horizontal posture with a tip payload of 10 kg, 1st joint achieved a high joint torque of 2797 Nm.</p></div></div><div class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1" id="S003"><h2 class="section-heading-2" id="d1e325">3.  Measurement of endpoint compliance</h2><p>This section demonstrates that Super Dragon has endpoint compliance due to the elasticity of driving tendons. First, we analytically show the compliance ellipsoid of the tip position, then measure the compliance value using the actual hardware and compare it with the analytical solution.</p><div class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2" id="S003-S2001"><h3 class="section-heading-3" id="d1e330">3.1.  Derivation of endpoint compliance ellipsoid</h3><p class="last">Let the tip position of Super&nbsp;Dragon in equilibrium state be <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img and the reaction force to its small displacement <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" Then, we define the stiffness coefficient matrix <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/22e7c59b-6ed8-487c-a665-673d8bc4d50b/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0007.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><msub><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">K</mi><mrow><mtext>x</mtext></mrow></msub><mo>∈</mo><msup><mrow><mi mathvariant="double-struck">R</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>3</mn><mo>×</mo><mn>3</mn></mrow></msup></math></span> of the arm tip by the following equation:
<span class="NLM_disp-formula-image disp-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" </span></span></span>Next, we define each joint torque of Super Dragon as <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">f</mi><mo>∈</mo><msup><mrow><mi We also define joint control tendon tension and gravity compensation tendon tension as <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/faff783f-6c86-4788-81d5-65d9dab6223e/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0010.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><msub><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">f</mi><mrow><mtext>j</mtext></mrow></msub><mo>∈</mo><msup><mrow><mi mathvariant="double-struck">R</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>20</mn><mo>×</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msup></math></span> and <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/044b6c80-6672-455a-a0a9-55a628dc7ad7/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0011.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><msub><mrow><mi>f</mi></mrow><mrow><mtext>wc</mtext></mrow></msub><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mi mathvariant="double-struck">R</mi></mrow></math></span>, respectively. We define the pulley matrix <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/b20731e7-da3f-4091-911a-91d9bb47bad3/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0012.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><msub><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">R</mi><mrow><mtext>j</mtext></mrow></msub><mo>∈</mo><msup><mrow><mi mathvariant="double-struck">R</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>10</mn><mo>×</mo><mn>20</mn></mrow></msup></math></span> regarding the pulley diameter and winding direction of joint control tendons. The component <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/aad748d1-8a84-469e-9cf1-f4b1efd9a01d/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0013.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><msub><mi>r</mi><mrow><mi>i</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>j</mi></mrow></msub></math></span> in the <i>i</i>-th row and <i>j</i>-th column of the pulley matrix represents the radius of the pulley around which rope <i>j</i> placed at the <i>i</i>-th joint is wound. The two ropes driving the <i>n</i>-th joint are designated as rope 2<i>n</i>−1 and rope <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/2e9954bd-784b-43e5-8553-f11911d86ce0/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0014.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><mn>2</mn><mi>n</mi></math></span>, wound to change the driven joint in negative and positive rotation directions, respectively. The radius of pulleys wound in the negative direction is taken as a negative value. Similarly, defining the pulley matrix for gravity compensation tendons as <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/5a24483c-64bc-4b4a-bda2-150d69055916/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0015.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><msub><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">R</mi><mrow><mtext>wc</mtext></mrow></msub><mo>∈</mo><msup><mrow><mi mathvariant="double-struck">R</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>10</mn><mo>×</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msup></math></span>, the joint torque <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/025204f9-073a-4025-9c05-efa7bf4af889/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0016.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">τ</mi></math></span> can be calculated as:

Also, we assume that the gravity compensation tendon tension <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/1a832c2e-bab3-42ff-bfdd-85f782054a15/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0027.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><msub><mi>f</mi><mrow><mtext>wc</mtext></mrow></msub></math></span> does not depend on <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/66cd62e8-2f5c-43c7-8edf-c9766db91709/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0028.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">θ</mi></math></span>. mathvariant="bold">⊤</mi></mrow></msup></math></span>, respectively. In redundant arms, generally <i>m</i>&lt;<i>n</i>, so pseudo-inverse matrices need to be used ; however, the pseudo-inverse matrices used in Equation&nbsp;(<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref disp-formula"><a data-rid="M0007" href="#" data-behaviour="toggle-ref" data-ref-type="disp-formula" data-label="equation"><span class="off-screen">Equation</span>7</a></span><span class="hidden" id="M0007"><span class="NLM_disp-formula-image disp-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/039231d8-ce13-42d1-bc8e-871b55cd83fb/tadr_a_2642632_m0007.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"><span class="disp_formula_label_div">(7) </span></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula disp-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><mtable columnalign="right left right left right left right left right left right left" columnspacing="0em 2em 0em 2em 0em 2em 0em 2em 0em 2em 0em" displaystyle="true" rowspacing="3pt"><mtr><mtd></mtd><mtd><msub><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">K</mi><mrow><mtext>x</mtext></mrow></msub><mo>=</mo><msup><mrow><mo>(</mo><msup><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">J</mi><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">⊤</mi></mrow></msup><mo>)</mo></mrow><mrow><mo>+</mo></mrow></msup><msub><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">R</mi><mrow><mtext>j</mtext></mrow></msub><msubsup><mrow><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">KR</mi></mrow><mrow><mtext>j</mtext></mrow><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">⊤</mi></mrow></msubsup><msup><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">J</mi><mrow><mo>+</mo></mrow></msup></mtd></mtr></mtable></math><span class="mathjaxLabel"><span class="disp_formula_label_div">(7) </span></span></span></span>) are not the most commonly used Moore-Penrose pseudo-inverse matrices. Since the row vectors of <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/b1ec0d87-e7e3-4b15-abed-72f903d30e7b/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0037.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">J</mi></math></span> are linearly independent and it is a wide matrix, there are infinitely many solutions to Equation&nbsp;(<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref disp-formula"><a data-rid="M0005" href="#" data-behaviour="toggle-ref" data-ref-type="disp-formula" data-label="equation"><span class="off-screen">Equation</span>5</a></span><span class="hidden" id="M0005"><span class="NLM_disp-formula-image disp-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/ef1dea41-e9a5-46d4-85d1-14e0b8a64081/tadr_a_2642632_m0005.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"><span class="disp_formula_label_div">(5) </span></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula disp-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><mtable columnalign="right left right left right left right left right left right left" columnspacing="0em 2em 0em 2em 0em 2em 0em 2em 0em 2em 0em" displaystyle="true" rowspacing="3pt"><mtr><mtd><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi><msub><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">x</mi><mrow><mtext>e</mtext></mrow></msub><mo>=</mo><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">J</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">θ</mi></mtd></mtr></mtable></math><span class="mathjaxLabel"><span class="disp_formula_label_div">(5) </span></span></span></span>). One solution, <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/ca9afbe4-35d1-4dae-bb39-5a5d7bdfa73b/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0038.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">θ</mi><mo>=</mo><msup><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">J</mi><mrow><mo>+</mo></mrow></msup><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi><msub><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">x</mi><mrow><mtext>e</mtext></mrow></msub></math></span> becomes the minimum norm solution when using the Moore-Penrose pseudo-inverse matrix. Since each joint stiffness differs in coupled tendon-driven arms, we use the Lagrange multiplier method to find the solution <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/607f7911-91cf-47d2-86f6-ec179e6d75e8/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0039.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">θ</mi></math></span> to Equation&nbsp;(<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref disp-formula"><a data-rid="M0005" href="#" data-behaviour="toggle-ref" data-ref-type="disp-formula" data-label="equation"><span class="off-screen">Equation</span>5</a></span><span class="hidden" id="M0005"><span class="NLM_disp-formula-image disp-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/ef1dea41-e9a5-46d4-85d1-14e0b8a64081/tadr_a_2642632_m0005.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"><span class="disp_formula_label_div">(5) </span></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula disp-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><mtable columnalign="right left right left right left right left right left right left" columnspacing="0em 2em 0em 2em 0em 2em 0em 2em 0em 2em 0em" displaystyle="true" rowspacing="3pt"><mtr><mtd><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi><msub><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">x</mi><mrow><mtext>e</mtext></mrow></msub><mo>=</mo><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">J</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">θ</mi></mtd></mtr></mtable></math><span class="mathjaxLabel"><span class="disp_formula_label_div">(5) </span></span></span></span>) that minimizes the sum of elastic energy <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/e8e7fd86-cc43-433a-bbd1-de4a77027356/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0040.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><msub><mi>E</mi><mrow><mtext>sum</mtext></mrow></msub></math></span> of each joint angle control tendon, thereby calculating the pseudo-inverse matrix. <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/6f389a1b-be10-44d7-8112-4d6a53a8b06f/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0041.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><msub><mi>E</mi><mrow><mtext>sum</mtext></mrow></msub></math></span> is as follows: Where <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/4f58dd7e-b2e8-4f80-87a8-6f70f27cd80a/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0042.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi><msub><mi>θ</mi><mrow><mi>j</mi></mrow></msub></math></span> is the <i>j</i>-th row component of <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/6a33fd20-09ed-42e7-bc6f-1145534f12e9/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0043.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">θ</mi></math></span>, and <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/22e89027-8137-403f-b08e-e930aa8cb481/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0044.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><msub><mi>K</mi><mrow><mi>i</mi></mrow></msub></math></span> represents the stiffness of rope <i>i</i>.
<span class="NLM_disp-formula-image disp-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/fd3417fa-caa1-46a7-a118-e81a984ee1dc/tadr_a_2642632_m0008.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"><span class="disp_formula_label_div">(8) </span></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula disp-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><mtable columnalign="right left right left right left right left right left right left" columnspacing="0em 2em 0em 2em 0em 2em 0em 2em 0em 2em 0em" displaystyle="true" rowspacing="3pt"><mtr><mtd><msub><mi>E</mi><mrow><mtext>sum</mtext></mrow></msub></mtd><mtd><mi></mi><mo>=</mo><munderover><mo>∑</mo><mrow><mi>i</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow><mrow><mi>n</mi></mrow></munderover><mrow><mo>(</mo><mfrac><mn>1</mn><mn>2</mn></mfrac><msub><mi>K</mi><mrow><mn>2</mn><mi>i</mi><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msub><msup><mrow><mo>(</mo><munderover><mo>∑</mo><mrow><mi>j</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow><mrow><mi>i</mi></mrow></munderover><msub><mi>r</mi><mrow><mi>j</mi><mo>,</mo><mn>2</mn><mi>i</mi><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msub><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi><msub><mi>θ</mi><mrow><mi>j</mi></mrow></msub><mo>)</mo></mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn></mrow></msup><mo fence="true" symmetric="true"></mo></mrow></mtd></mtr><mtr><mtd></mtd><mtd><mspace width="1em"></mspace><mrow><mo fence="true" symmetric="true"></mo><mo>+</mo><mfrac><mn>1</mn><mn>2</mn></mfrac><msub><mi>K</mi><mrow><mn>2</mn><mi>i</mi></mrow></msub><msup><mrow><mo>(</mo><munderover><mo>∑</mo><mrow><mi>j</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow><mrow><mi>i</mi></mrow></munderover><msub><mi>r</mi><mrow><mi>j</mi><mo>,</mo><mn>2</mn><mi>i</mi></mrow></msub><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi><msub><mi>θ</mi><mrow><mi>j</mi></mrow></msub><mo>)</mo></mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn></mrow></msup><mo>)</mo></mrow></mtd></mtr></mtable></math><span class="mathjaxLabel"><span class="disp_formula_label_div">(8) </span></span></span>In this paper, we consider the endpoint compliance ellipsoid of Super Dragon in horizontal posture (<span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/0378ec00-6fab-4b53-8286-ec8ed4fc403c/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0045.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">θ</mi><mo>=</mo><mn mathvariant="bold">0</mn></math></span>). Unlike general postures, the horizontal posture is a singular posture, so the endpoint compliance has no component in the longitudinal direction, i.e. the <i>x</i>-axis direction. Therefore, the endpoint compliance ellipsoid in horizontal posture becomes a two-dimensional ellipse that can be drawn in <i>yz</i> coordinates, as shown in Figure&nbsp;<button class="ref show-table-fig-ref" data-id="F0004" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-popup-event-type="fig">4</button> drawn using MATLAB. Here, we ignore the influence of gravity compensation tendons because the base-side joints where gravity compensation tendons are wound have high joint stiffness due to many tendons being wound around them, resulting in relatively small joint angle changes at the base side when displacement. We assume that the elastic coefficient of joint control tendons is constant regardless of elongation, and set the elastic coefficient per unit strain as <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/818a1daa-e45f-4fbd-bea4-7069f305fb66/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0046.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><mi>k</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>3.40</mn><mo>×</mo><msup><mn>10</mn><mrow><mn>4</mn></mrow></msup><mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">N</mi></mrow></math></span>. The measurement and derivation of this value are described in the Appendix. Furthermore, assuming quasi-static motion, we ignore the viscosity coefficient. As shown in Figure <button class="ref show-table-fig-ref" data-id="F0004" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-popup-event-type="fig">4</button>, the ellipse axis does not coincide with the <i>y</i> and <i>z</i> axes but is tilted. The angle between the major axis of the ellipse and the <i>y</i>-axis is <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/d1e76372-dfc5-4321-aff8-009fabeac1d4/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0047.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><mn>8.6</mn><mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace><mtext>deg</mtext></math></span>. For a typical robot arm consisting of pitch and yaw joints in horizontal posture, the two axes of the endpoint compliance ellipsoid coincide with the rotation axes of pitch or yaw joints in horizontal posture. However, in coupled tendon drive, the ellipse tilts because joint angle changes affect joints with different rotation axes.
</p><div class="figureView"><div class="short-legend"><p class="captionText"><span aria-level="3" role="heading"><span class="captionLabel">Figure 4. </span></span> Calculated compliance ellipse.</p></div><a href="#" class="thumbnail" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-popup-event-type="fig" data-id="F0004"><img id="d1e1452" src="/cms/asset/2d68c69f-5f68-46c1-a2d4-e546ea587802/tadr_a_2642632_f0004_oc.jpg" loading="lazy" height="422" width="500" alt="Figure 4. Calculated compliance ellipse."></a><div><button class="show-full-size btn btn-sm" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-id="F0004" data-popup-event-type="fig">Display full size</button></div></div><p></p></div><div class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2" id="S003-S2002"><h3 class="section-heading-3" id="d1e1455">3.2.  Endpoint compliance measurement experiment</h3><p>We conducted an endpoint compliance measurement experiment in horizontal posture to verify the validity of the previous section. The experiment was conducted by stopping the base motors with Super Dragon maintained horizontally. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<button class="ref show-table-fig-ref" data-id="F0005" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-popup-event-type="fig">5</button>, the experiment was conducted by connecting a force gauge (Nidec-Shimpo: FGP-50) to the Super Dragon's tip with a rope, and measuring the tension when pulling and releasing in both positive and negative directions along the <i>y</i>-axis and <i>z</i>-axis. The tip position was measured by driving the force gauge at a constant speed using a linear stage (COMS: PM40B-25X) and reading the tension at regular time intervals, measuring the tip position twice in each of the four directions along the <i>y</i> and <i>z</i> axes. Here, since rope elongation occurs due to pulling the arm tip and the passage of time, increasing the joint angle error from the horizontal posture, we corrected the joint angles to horizontal posture after two experiments in each direction. The movement speed of the linear stage was <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/a82ec56c-63d2-418c-b2bb-8ce1efd1fe3f/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0048.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><mn>1</mn><mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace><mrow><mtext>mm/s</mtext></mrow></math></span> for the first measurement in the <i>y</i>-axis positive direction and <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/eb388853-ea01-4f97-948d-ccde07558b50/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0049.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><mn>2</mn><mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace><mrow><mtext>mm/s</mtext></mrow></math></span> for all others.
</p><div class="figureView"><div class="short-legend"><p class="captionText"><span aria-level="3" role="heading"><span class="captionLabel">Figure 5. </span></span> Compliance measurement experiment (<i>y</i>-axis positive direction).</p></div><a href="#" class="thumbnail" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-popup-event-type="fig" data-id="F0005"><img id="d1e1509" src="/cms/asset/5641dcd7-01e0-4c7f-9f78-eddc3bbc4b0a/tadr_a_2642632_f0005_oc.jpg" loading="lazy" height="329" width="500" alt="Figure 5. Compliance measurement experiment (y-axis positive direction)."></a><div><button class="show-full-size btn btn-sm" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-id="F0005" data-popup-event-type="fig">Display full size</button></div></div><p></p><p>The measurement results from the rise of tension to maximum tension were taken as the measurement results. Next, the measurement results were linearly approximated using the least squares method (<span class="monospace">polyfit</span> function, Matlab). The data are displayed such that the line for pulling passes through the origin, and the line for releasing intersects at the position of maximum tension (Figures&nbsp;<button class="ref show-table-fig-ref" data-id="F0006" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-popup-event-type="fig">6</button> and&nbsp;<button class="ref show-table-fig-ref" data-id="F0007" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-popup-event-type="fig">7</button>). Figure <button class="ref show-table-fig-ref" data-id="F0006" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-popup-event-type="fig">6</button> shows the measurement results in the <i>y</i>-axis positive direction and <i>y</i>-axis negative direction from top to bottom, with the first and second measurements shown from left to right for each direction. Similarly, Figure <button class="ref show-table-fig-ref" data-id="F0007" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-popup-event-type="fig">7</button> shows the measurement results in the <i>z</i>-axis direction. The average value of the measured slopes in each data set was taken as the tip stiffness. By taking the reciprocal, the compliance in the <i>y</i> and <i>z</i>-axis directions was calculated as 31.8 and <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/c31dccc8-7a86-452f-896f-fd0e404f7644/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0050.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><mn>22.6</mn><mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace><mrow><mtext>mm/N</mtext></mrow></math></span>, respectively.
</p><div class="figureView"><div class="short-legend"><p class="captionText"><span aria-level="3" role="heading"><span class="captionLabel">Figure 6. </span></span> Result of compliance measurement in <i>y</i>-direction. The measurement data obtained from the force gauge are displayed as scatter plots. The dashed lines indicate approximate lines obtained by linearly approximating the measurement data.</p><p class="captionText">Left side: 1st measurement. Right side: 2nd measurement.</p></div><a href="#" class="thumbnail" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-popup-event-type="fig" data-id="F0006"><img id="d1e1565" src="/cms/asset/d5ab35e3-77e1-4764-b030-6ad4f34adce7/tadr_a_2642632_f0006_oc.jpg" loading="lazy" height="500" width="486" alt="Figure 6. Result of compliance measurement in y-direction. The measurement data obtained from the force gauge are displayed as scatter plots. The dashed lines indicate approximate lines obtained by linearly approximating the measurement data.Left side: 1st measurement. Right side: 2nd measurement."></a><div><button class="show-full-size btn btn-sm" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-id="F0006" data-popup-event-type="fig">Display full size</button></div></div>
<div class="figureView"><div class="short-legend"><p class="captionText"><span aria-level="3" role="heading"><span class="captionLabel">Figure 7. </span></span> Result of compliance measurement in <i>z</i>-direction.The measurement data obtained from the force gauge are displayed as scatter plots. The dashed lines indicate approximate lines obtained by linearly approximating the measurement data.</p><p class="captionText">Left side: 1st measurement. Right side: 2nd measurement.</p></div><a href="#" class="thumbnail" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-popup-event-type="fig" data-id="F0007"><img id="d1e1579" src="/cms/asset/347b6af6-9c6a-4c65-9aa9-b501775289dd/tadr_a_2642632_f0007_oc.jpg" loading="lazy" height="500" width="493" alt="Figure 7. Result of compliance measurement in z-direction.The measurement data obtained from the force gauge are displayed as scatter plots. The dashed lines indicate approximate lines obtained by linearly approximating the measurement data.Left side: 1st measurement. Right side: 2nd measurement."></a><div><button class="show-full-size btn btn-sm" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-id="F0007" data-popup-event-type="fig">Display full size</button></div></div><p></p><p>We compare the joint angle changes when pulled 0.2 m in the first measurements in the <i>y</i>-axis positive direction and <i>z</i>-axis positive direction with the analytical results. The analytical calculation method for joint angles uses the pseudo-inverse matrix of the Jacobian matrix derived as shown in Section&nbsp;<a href="#S003-S2001" data-behaviour="scroll" data-behaviour-ref="#S003-S2001" data-behaviour-callback="focus" data-behaviour-callback-target="#S003-S2001">3.1</a> for Equation&nbsp;(<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref disp-formula"><a data-rid="M0005" href="#" data-behaviour="toggle-ref" data-ref-type="disp-formula" data-label="equation"><span class="off-screen">Equation</span>5</a></span><span class="hidden" id="M0005"><span class="NLM_disp-formula-image disp-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/ef1dea41-e9a5-46d4-85d1-14e0b8a64081/tadr_a_2642632_m0005.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"><span class="disp_formula_label_div">(5) </span></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula disp-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><mtable columnalign="right left right left right left right left right left right left" columnspacing="0em 2em 0em 2em 0em 2em 0em 2em 0em 2em 0em" displaystyle="true" rowspacing="3pt"><mtr><mtd><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi><msub><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">x</mi><mrow><mtext>e</mtext></mrow></msub><mo>=</mo><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">J</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">θ</mi></mtd></mtr></mtable></math><span class="mathjaxLabel"><span class="disp_formula_label_div">(5) </span></span></span></span>) to calculate the joint angle changes when giving 0.2 m displacement in the <i>y</i> and <i>z</i>-axis directions, respectively. The measured values and analytical results are shown in Table&nbsp;<button class="ref show-table-fig-ref" data-id="T0001" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-popup-event-type="table">1</button>.
</p><div class="tableView"><div class="tableCaption"><div class="short-legend"><h3><p class="captionText"><span class="captionLabel">Table 1. </span> Joint angle changes and analytical results in compliance measurement experiments.</p></h3></div></div><div class="tableDownloadOption" id="T0001-table-wrapper"><a data-id="T0001" class="downloadButton btn btn-sm displaySizeTable" href="#" role="button" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-popup-event-type="table">Display Table</a></div></div><p></p><p class="last">We compare these results with the analytical results from the previous section. The intersection point on the horizontal axis (labeled <i>y</i>-axis compliance) of the endpoint compliance ellipsoid shown in Figure <button class="ref show-table-fig-ref" data-id="F0004" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-popup-event-type="fig">4</button> indicates the compliance when force is applied laterally to the arm tip. Similarly, the compliance in the <i>z</i>-axis direction can be obtained, with the compliance in the <i>y</i>-axis and <i>z</i>-axis directions being 315 and <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/74753928-e135-44a8-86c8-85b95c47fb1a/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0061.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><mn>234</mn><mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace><mrow><mtext>mm/N</mtext></mrow></math></span>, respectively. These results are shown in Figure&nbsp;<button class="ref show-table-fig-ref" data-id="F0008" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-popup-event-type="fig">8</button>. The blue bars represent the analytical values of endpoint compliance obtained in Section&nbsp;<a href="#S003-S2001" data-behaviour="scroll" data-behaviour-ref="#S003-S2001" data-behaviour-callback="focus" data-behaviour-callback-target="#S003-S2001">3.1</a>, and the red bars represent the measured values obtained from measurement experiments. In contrast, as shown in Section&nbsp;<a href="#S003-S2003" data-behaviour="scroll" data-behaviour-ref="#S003-S2003" data-behaviour-callback="focus" data-behaviour-callback-target="#S003-S2003">3.3</a>, the analytical values of endpoint compliance obtained using the equivalent tendon stiffness <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/1c474205-ff31-4e96-a91d-a8723df924b3/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0062.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><msub><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">K</mi><mrow><mtext>exp</mtext></mrow></msub></math></span> including frictional forces acting on the rope are shown in green. The measured values compared to the analytical solutions were <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/d84497ef-0045-450b-b83a-711c6dc5697f/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0063.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><mn>9.91</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></math></span> in the <i>y</i>-axis direction and <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/9dfc47b4-76d1-4668-a815-d67fd8f018cb/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0064.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><mn>10.4</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></math></span> in the <i>z</i>-axis direction, showing lower compliance in the measured values but confirming that the order of magnitude matches.
</p><div class="figureView"><div class="short-legend"><p class="captionText"><span aria-level="3" role="heading"><span class="captionLabel">Figure 8. </span></span> The analytical solution and measured values of endpoint compliance in the <i>y</i>-axis and <i>z</i>-axis. Blue: The analytical solution using <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/91eea01b-7852-4df4-afb5-cbbc5a8c7cdf/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0065.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><msub><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">K</mi><mrow><mtext>sim</mtext></mrow></msub></math></span>. Green: The analytical solution using <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/c08b3be8-a2f3-447b-b54c-a795c40f8fca/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0066.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><msub><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">K</mi><mrow><mtext>exp</mtext></mrow></msub></math></span>. Red: Measured values.</p></div><a href="#" class="thumbnail" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-popup-event-type="fig" data-id="F0008"><img id="d1e1943" src="/cms/asset/68849124-d5fb-4463-be31-5d0b3dd8d76a/tadr_a_2642632_f0008_oc.jpg" loading="lazy" height="332" width="500" alt="Figure 8. The analytical solution and measured values of endpoint compliance in the y-axis and z-axis. Blue: The analytical solution using Ksim. Green: The analytical solution using Kexp. Red: Measured values."></a><div><button class="show-full-size btn btn-sm" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-id="F0008" data-popup-event-type="fig">Display full size</button></div></div><p></p></div><div class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2" id="S003-S2003"><h3 class="section-heading-3" id="d1e1946">3.3.  Consideration</h3><p>We discuss the results from the previous section. As shown in Figure <button class="ref show-table-fig-ref" data-id="F0008" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-popup-event-type="fig">8</button>, the measured endpoint compliance values are approximately 10% of the analytically obtained values. The cause of such numerical differences is considered to be the influence of frictional forces acting on the joint control tendons. In Section&nbsp;<a href="#S003-S2001" data-behaviour="scroll" data-behaviour-ref="#S003-S2001" data-behaviour-callback="focus" data-behaviour-callback-target="#S003-S2001">3.1</a>, the analysis was performed under the assumption that tension is uniformly distributed along the rope with respect to elongation. However, in reality, the rope tension is not uniformly distributed due to rotational friction at pulleys where the rope is wound around and frictional forces arising from contact with the rope itself at sections wound around pulleys. The non-uniform distribution of rope tension may have resulted in the measured values showing smaller compliance. Here, we consider calculating the equivalent stiffness of the joint control tendons using joint angular displacement data and tension data obtained from logs in the endpoint compliance measurement experiment presented in Section&nbsp;<a href="#S003-S2002" data-behaviour="scroll" data-behaviour-ref="#S003-S2002" data-behaviour-callback="focus" data-behaviour-callback-target="#S003-S2002">3.2</a>. If higher tension than expected was acting due to frictional forces, the obtained joint control tendon stiffness represents an equivalent stiffness that includes the influence of friction. Therefore, we calculate the equivalent stiffness of each joint control tendon obtained from compliance measurements and re-analytically determine the endpoint compliance based on this to investigate the influence of frictional forces acting on the rope on endpoint compliance.</p><p>Here, we calculate the equivalent stiffness of joint control tendons based on joint angle and tension data from the compliance measurement experiment in the positive <i>z</i>-axis direction. The reason for focusing on <i>z</i>-axis direction measurements is that most of Super Dragon's joints are pitch joints, and more joint control tendons are expected to influence the results compared to the <i>y</i>-axis direction, thus yielding more accurate results. Since all the actuators were completely stopped, elongation <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/6ebd2b81-ebdd-4a40-8b80-daf0a5f6303b/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0067.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">l</mi></math></span> occurs in each joint control tendon solely due to joint angular displacement caused by pulling the arm's endpoint. The elongation <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/2bc72803-adc9-44e3-8f94-eed78bb609e4/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0068.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">l</mi></math></span> can be expressed as <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/b96d0819-5908-4140-a591-2794f7fcbfd7/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0069.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">l</mi><mo>=</mo><msubsup><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">R</mi><mrow><mtext>j</mtext></mrow><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">⊤</mi></mrow></msubsup><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">θ</mi></math></span> using joint angular displacement data <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/4bcdab84-6e6d-4872-8818-8a1a5c2ba509/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0070.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">θ</mi></math></span> and the pulley matrix <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/95c60b1b-e0f7-4e3d-9a0d-cffde82559d4/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0071.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><msub><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">R</mi><mrow><mtext>j</mtext></mrow></msub></math></span>. Note that the elongation <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/c8e5c957-232c-4c27-b73b-f9f63f65b8a7/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0072.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">l</mi></math></span> here represents the elongation from the initial horizontal posture and differs from the elongation from the natural length of each joint control tendon. Linear interpolation was performed on the experimentally obtained elongation <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/f21d7331-b805-44c3-967d-5c332f251a57/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0073.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">l</mi></math></span> [m] and tension <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/49913bcd-604f-48ad-b7f6-103f01a232b0/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0074.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">f</mi></math></span> [N] data (<span class="monospace">polyfit</span> function, Matlab) to obtain an equivalent stiffness matrix including the effects of friction, denoted as <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/1291c643-df91-4aca-ac72-1567d1e57b41/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0075.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><msub><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">K</mi><mrow><mtext>exp</mtext></mrow></msub></math></span> [N/m]. Here, multiplying the diagonal components of <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/449efc44-1b0c-4046-9093-f3776260d06a/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0076.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><msub><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">K</mi><mrow><mtext>exp</mtext></mrow></msub></math></span> by the natural length of each rope yields the strain stiffness <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/bf06de00-d1b6-4035-9dc9-f8738e896f32/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0077.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><msub><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">k</mi><mrow><mtext>exp</mtext></mrow></msub></math></span>. However, it is difficult to measure all unloaded tendon lengths in advance for Super Dragon, where numerous tendons are wound around pulleys. Additionally, when the arm is maintained in a horizontal posture, joint control tendons experience tensions up to approximately 1000 N, but the resulting elongation from the unloaded state is considered sufficiently small compared to rope lengths on the order of several meters. Therefore, in this paper, we multiply the equivalent stiffness <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/49c20edc-975a-4fe0-9838-7ebb321337bd/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0078.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><msub><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">K</mi><mrow><mtext>exp</mtext></mrow></msub></math></span> of the joint control tendons by the rope length of the joint control tendons in the horizontal posture, and treat the obtained approximate values as the strain stiffness <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/57a25a4e-2a60-4d98-927c-a0816982c709/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0079.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><msub><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">k</mi><mrow><mtext>exp</mtext></mrow></msub></math></span>.</p><p>Each component of the obtained <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/48f6f93f-e5ec-49cb-a14c-40c042f2ac21/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0080.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><msub><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">k</mi><mrow><mtext>exp</mtext></mrow></msub></math></span> is shown in Figure&nbsp;<button class="ref show-table-fig-ref" data-id="F0009" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-popup-event-type="fig">9</button>. Rope numbers follow the convention where the two ropes driving the <i>n</i>-th joint are designated as ropes 2<i>n</i>−1 and <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/a9d350fd-de25-4e7e-bf42-a788ecf34ca6/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0081.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><mn>2</mn><mi>n</mi></math></span>. Graphs for pitch joint control tendons are shown in magenta, and those for yaw joint control tendons in cyan. The strain stiffness value <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/77c25167-ab4f-44e8-a41b-f7c2aae0649a/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0082.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><mi>k</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>3.40</mn><mo>×</mo><msup><mn>10</mn><mrow><mn>4</mn></mrow></msup><mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">N</mi></mrow></math></span> used in the analysis in Section&nbsp;<a href="#S003-S2001" data-behaviour="scroll" data-behaviour-ref="#S003-S2001" data-behaviour-callback="focus" data-behaviour-callback-target="#S003-S2001">3.1</a> is indicated by a black dashed line. As can be seen from Figure <button class="ref show-table-fig-ref" data-id="F0009" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-popup-event-type="fig">9</button>, joint control tendons closer to the base show values closer to <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/38ecbce1-b9fa-4d18-9adf-b2d13405bd20/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0083.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><mi>k</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>3.40</mn><mo>×</mo><msup><mn>10</mn><mrow><mn>4</mn></mrow></msup><mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">N</mi></mrow></math></span>, while those on the tip side, which are wound around more pulleys, tend to show larger values. Thus, it was newly found that frictional forces acting on the rope increase measured tension values and contribute to increased equivalent stiffness.
</p><div class="figureView"><div class="short-legend"><p class="captionText"><span aria-level="3" role="heading"><span class="captionLabel">Figure 9. </span></span> Equivalent strain stiffness including the effect of friction force acting on joint control tendons.</p></div><a href="#" class="thumbnail" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-popup-event-type="fig" data-id="F0009"><img id="d1e2202" src="/cms/asset/331a0ff5-56f9-404e-8906-a0444bb3ef74/tadr_a_2642632_f0009_oc.jpg" loading="lazy" height="239" width="500" alt="Figure 9. Equivalent strain stiffness including the effect of friction force acting on joint control tendons."></a><div><button class="show-full-size btn btn-sm" data-behaviour="show-popup" data-id="F0009" data-popup-event-type="fig">Display full size</button></div></div><p></p><p>Using the obtained <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;image&quot;,&quot;src&quot;:&quot;/cms/asset/1d91eb10-5ab9-4825-93fc-34457a5fdc83/tadr_a_2642632_ilm0084.gif&quot;}"></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;mathjax&quot;}"><math><msub><mi mathvariant="bold-italic">K</mi><mrow><mtext>exp</mtext></mrow></msub></math></span>, we calculate the endpoint compliance using Equation&nbsp;(<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref disp-formula"><a data-rid="M0007" href="#" data-behaviour="toggle-ref" data-ref-type="disp-formula" data-label="equation"><span class="off-screen">Equation</span>7</a></span><span class="hidden" id="M0007"><span class="NLM_disp-formula-image disp-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula"
